<div id="review_2809881475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2809881475" />
    <a title="Bulent Erdemir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8046999-bulent-erdemir"><img alt="Bulent Erdemir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467901388p2/8046999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2809881475?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bulent Erdemir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bulent Erdemir" href="/user/show/8046999-bulent-erdemir">Bulent Erdemir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2809881475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10649708518764774714">The author created a dystopian future which is very nice to read. The book is short, maybe as a result of this, the characters and the story is not well developed. As the reader, you in fact expect more from the book and the plot overall could have been mode sophisticated. However, it's worth a read just to witness the mind bending that's in the story. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_31265764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31265764" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31265764?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31265764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2799738622901327259">This 1971 offering from Polish author Stanislaw Lem mixes black humour, absurdism, and social satire brilliantly in a short novel that will make you laugh at times, and make you think always. <br/>The Futurological Congress follows one of the adventures of character Ijon Tichy as he is caught up in a chemical attack. The book provides satire on both the social move towards a "chemically corrected society" where we use different drugs to fix any kind of problem we encounter, and a more subtle commenta</span>
  <span id="freeText2799738622901327259" style="display:none">This 1971 offering from Polish author Stanislaw Lem mixes black humour, absurdism, and social satire brilliantly in a short novel that will make you laugh at times, and make you think always. <br />The Futurological Congress follows one of the adventures of character Ijon Tichy as he is caught up in a chemical attack. The book provides satire on both the social move towards a "chemically corrected society" where we use different drugs to fix any kind of problem we encounter, and a more subtle commentary on Lem's perception of the idiocy and deceit of government.<br />An excellent book that could be described as Huxley meets Dahli, definately worth reading!</span>

<div id="review_622658528" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622658528" />
    <a title="Joshua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/646605-joshua"><img alt="Joshua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417806196p2/646605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/622658528?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua" href="/user/show/646605-joshua">Joshua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780380005840" href="/book/show/1282668.The_Futurological_Congress">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/646605-joshua?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622658528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6006069314653512287">A very wild read. Multiple dystopian visions couched in nested hallucinations instigated by chemical warfare within another dystopia. The plot is fairly unsubstantial, but the book is short, so that's not really a problem. The story is really just Lem running wild with a thought experiment. I found it particularly fascinating to read having just finished Daniel Dennett's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2069.Consciousness_Explained' rel='nofollow noopener'>Consciousness Explained</a>.<br/><br/>What is possibly most impressive is the translation. This book has a running theme about technical neo</span>
  <span id="freeText6006069314653512287" style="display:none">A very wild read. Multiple dystopian visions couched in nested hallucinations instigated by chemical warfare within another dystopia. The plot is fairly unsubstantial, but the book is short, so that's not really a problem. The story is really just Lem running wild with a thought experiment. I found it particularly fascinating to read having just finished Daniel Dennett's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2069.Consciousness_Explained" rel="nofollow noopener">Consciousness Explained</a>.<br /><br />What is possibly most impressive is the translation. This book has a running theme about technical neologisms, and despite having been written in Polish, the wordplay throughout the English version is quite fun and feels as though it were originally written in English. I am not familiar with Polish, so I don't know how well the one language lends itself to cognates in the other, but I found myself impressed with how well the story makes fun of English word combinations. There are way too many examples of the delicious wordplay to give it proper summary here, so I'll just conclude this review with my favorite, "lubricrat": one who gives bribes, derived from the greasing of palms. I think I will start using this term to describe modern day corporate lobbyists.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6006069314653512287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1477235247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16912753731853949159">I rate Stanislaw Lem as I rate Philip K. Dick, which is to say, very highly indeed. I recently read that his work is being newly translated, these editions being far superior to the ones I owned in my youth. However, I’m on a mission to rebuild the collection I had back then, so restricted myself to this 1974 copy, which adorned my shelves too many decades ago. In THE FUTUROLOGICAL CONGRESS, Lem immediately plunges the reader into a world of overcrowding, sexual excess, and terrorism, where a ha</span>
  <span id="freeText16912753731853949159" style="display:none">I rate Stanislaw Lem as I rate Philip K. Dick, which is to say, very highly indeed. I recently read that his work is being newly translated, these editions being far superior to the ones I owned in my youth. However, I’m on a mission to rebuild the collection I had back then, so restricted myself to this 1974 copy, which adorned my shelves too many decades ago. In THE FUTUROLOGICAL CONGRESS, Lem immediately plunges the reader into a world of overcrowding, sexual excess, and terrorism, where a hapless convention guest finds himself caught up in a drug-fuelled revolution, hallucinating wildly, only to eventually wake up in the year 2039, where practically every experience imaginable can be had in pill form. This novel is brimming with satire, breathtakingly inventive, and so surrealistic and psychedelic that it makes your head spin. Wonderful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16912753731853949159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f9QrwPiydnq0i5HNleuxoGtVre87QMFGpq/QcIKSHAeCWHFrPtiQk3+lb4zQcF7q1ZBcBbYzZz2Cx+WB9yycqQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sW9OpReZBX1onAieefFGInUe2TmiEaRHkr7rru9AK1NM4xQO0fPjlKOy9t88aqloy9so0y9iAjy21t5fmv6r/Q==')})
  }

In a glass-en<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8207898329202225183\" style=\"display:none\">The exhilarating dystopian novel that inspired George Orwell\'s 1984 and foreshadowed the worst excesses of Soviet Russia\n\nYevgeny Zamyatin\'s We is a powerfully inventive vision that has influenced writers from George Orwell to Ayn Rand. In a glass-enclosed city of absolute straight lines, ruled over by the all-powerful \'Benefactor\', the citizens of the totalitarian society of OneState live out lives devoid of passion and creativity - until D-503, a mathematician who dreams in numbers, makes a discovery: he has an individual soul. Set in the twenty-sixth century AD, We is the classic dystopian novel and was the forerunner of works such as George Orwell\'s 1984 and Aldous Huxley\'s Brave New World. It was suppressed for many years in Russia and remains a resounding cry for individual freedom, yet is also a powerful, exciting and vivid work of science fiction. Originally published in Poland in 1937. Ferdydurke became an instant literary sensation and catapulted the young author to fame. Deemed scandalous and subversive by Nazis. Stalinists. and the Polish Communist regime in turn. the novel (as well as all of Gombrowicz\'s other works) was officially banned in Poland for decades. It has nonetheless remained one of the most influential works of twentieth-century European literature.  Ferdydurke is translated here directly from the Polish for the first time.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10991.Stanis_aw_Lem">About Stanisław Lem</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/10991.Stanis_aw_Lem"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1246185166p3/10991.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/10991.Stanis_aw_Lem">Stanisław Lem
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10098975776639193778">Stanisław Lem (staˈɲiswaf lɛm) was a Polish science fiction, philosophical and satirical writer of Jewish descent. His books have been translated into 41 languages and have sold over 27 million copies. He is perhaps best known as the author of <i>Solaris</i>, which has twice been made into a feature film. In 1976, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12531.Theodore_Sturgeon' title='Theodore Sturgeon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Theodore Sturgeon</a> claimed that Lem was the most widely read science-fiction writer in the w</span>
  <span id="freeText10098975776639193778" style="display:none">Stanisław Lem (staˈɲiswaf lɛm) was a Polish science fiction, philosophical and satirical writer of Jewish descent. His books have been translated into 41 languages and have sold over 27 million copies. He is perhaps best known as the author of <i>Solaris</i>, which has twice been made into a feature film. In 1976, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12531.Theodore_Sturgeon" title="Theodore Sturgeon" rel="nofollow noopener">Theodore Sturgeon</a> claimed that Lem was the most widely read science-fiction writer in the world.<br /><br />His works explore philosophical themes; speculation on technology, the nature of intelligence, the impossibility of mutual communication and understanding, despair about human limitations and humankind's place in the universe. They are sometimes presented as fiction, but others are in the form of essays or philosophical books. Translations of his works are difficult and multiple translated versions of his works exist.<br /><br />Lem became truly productive after 1956, when the de-Stalinization period led to the "Polish October", when Poland experienced an increase in freedom of speech. Between 1956 and 1968, Lem authored 17 books. His works were widely translated abroad (although mostly in the Eastern Bloc countries). In 1957 he published his first non-fiction, philosophical book, <i>Dialogi</i> (Dialogues), one of his two most famous philosophical texts along with <i>Summa Technologiae</i> (1964). The Summa is notable for being a unique analysis of prospective social, cybernetic, and biological advances. In this work, Lem discusses philosophical implications of technologies that were completely in the realm of science fiction then, but are gaining importance today—like, for instance, virtual reality and nanotechnology. Over the next few decades, he published many books, both science fiction and philosophical/futurological, although from the 1980s onwards he tended to concentrate on philosophical texts and essays.<br /><br />He gained international fame for <i>The Cyberiad</i>, a series of humorous short stories from a mechanical universe ruled by robots, first published in English in 1974. His best-known novels include <i>Solaris</i> (1961), <i>His Master's Voice</i> (Głos pana, 1968), and the late <i>Fiasco</i> (Fiasko, 1987), expressing most strongly his major theme of the futility of mankind's attempts to comprehend the truly alien. Solaris was made into a film in 1972 by Russian director Andrei Tarkovsky and won a Special Jury Prize at the Cannes Film Festival in 1972; in 2002, Steven Soderbergh directed a Hollywood remake starring George Clooney.<br /><br />He was the cousin of poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5565396.Marian_Hemar" title="Marian Hemar" rel="nofollow noopener">Marian Hemar</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10098975776639193778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
